     221             : // If a window with the given bound in some dimension is dilated with the given
     222             : // dilation factor in that dimension, then the value returned is the bound for
     223             : // the array in that dimension after dilation.
     224             : //
     225             : // For a 1D array with 3 entries 1, 2, 3, a dilation factor of 2 yields a new
     226             : // window with values 1, x, 2, x, 3, where x indicates holes left by the
     227             : // dilation. So DilatedBound(3, 2) == 5.
     228        8280 : int64_t dilatedBound(int64_t bound, int64_t dilation) {
     229        8280 :   assert(bound >= 0 && "The dimension to dialate must be >= 0");
     230        8280 :   if (bound == 0) return 0;
     231             : 
     232             :   // Suppose the array has three entries 123 and the dilation factor is 4. Then
     233             :   // the dilated array has 9 entries 1xxx2xxx3. Here, each original entry except
     234             :   // the last expands into 4 entries, so that is (bound - 1) * dilation. Then we
     235             :   // add 1 to account for the final input element.
     236        8280 :   return (bound - 1) * dilation + 1;
     237        8280 : }
     238             : 
     239             : // Returns the number of valid positions of a window with the given size and
     240             : // stride within an array with the given bound. This is the bound of an output
     241             : // array with one element per valid position of the window.
     242             : //
     243             : // For example, for arguments of (bound=5, window_size=2, stride=2), the
     244             : // returned value is 2. There are valid positions at offset 0 and offset 2,
     245             : // while offset 4 is not valid since the window's last entry would be at 5,
     246             : // which is beyond the bound of 5.
     247        4143 : int64_t stridedBound(int64_t bound, int64_t windowSize, int64_t stride) {
     248        4143 :   assert(windowSize >= 0 && "Expected window size to be >= 0");
     249        4143 :   assert(bound >= 0 && "Expected bound to be >= 0");
     250             : 
     251        4141 :   if (bound == 0 || windowSize > bound) return 0;
     252             : 
     253             :   // Without considering stride, the maximum valid offset is bound -
     254             :   // window_size. Taking stride into account, the valid offsets then have the
     255             :   // form q * stride for q = 0, ..., Q such that q * stride <= bound -
     256             :   // window_size. This implies that Q equals floor(bound - window_size /
     257             :   // stride). There are Q + 1 valid values of q, yielding the formula below.
     258        4141 :   return (bound - windowSize) / stride + 1;
     259        4141 : }
     260             :

     435             : 
     436             :   // Consider typical reduce-* op syntax:
     437             :   //
     438             :   //      op(I(i), V(j)):
     439             :   //       block(BI(i), BV(j)):
     440             :   //         ... some computation ...
     441             :   //         return(R(i))
     442             :   //
     443             :   // where
     444             :   //  I(i)  : i-th input of op
     445             :   //  V(j)  : j-th init-value of op
     446             :   //  BI(i) : i-th input of reducer-function
     447             :   //  BV(j) : j-th init-value of reducer-function
     448             :   //  R(i)  : i-th return-type
     449             :   //
     450             :   //  Note that: |I(i)| == |V(j)| == |BI(i)| == |BV(j)| == |R(i)|
     451             :   //

    1281             : 
    1282             : namespace {
    1283             : 
    1284             : // following https://www.tensorflow.org/xla/operation_semantics#gather
    1285             : // The bounds for the output array along dimension i is computed as follows:
    1286             : // (1) If i is present in batch_dims (i.e. is equal to batch_dims[k] for some k)
    1287             : // then we pick
    1288             : // the corresponding dimension bounds out of start_indices.shape, skipping
    1289             : // index_vector_dim
    1290             : // (i.e. pick start_indices.shape.dims[k] if k < index_vector_dim and
    1291             : // start_indices.shape.dims[k+1] otherwise).
    1292             : // (2) If i is present in offset_dims (i.e. equal to offset_dims[k] for some k)
    1293             : // then we pick
    1294             : // the corresponding bound out of slice_sizes after accounting for
    1295             : // collapsed_slice_dims
    1296             : // (i.e. we pick adjusted_slice_sizes[k] where adjusted_slice_sizes is
    1297             : // slice_sizes with the bounds at indices collapsed_slice_dims removed).
    1298             : 
    1299           0 : void getSliceSizeValues(GatherOp* gather, OpBuilder& builder, Location loc,
    1300             :                         ValueRange operands,
    1301           0 :                         SmallVectorImpl<Value>& sliceSizes) {
    1302           0 :   for (int64_t val : gather->slice_sizes().getValues<int64_t>()) {
    1303           0 :     sliceSizes.push_back(builder.create<arith::ConstantIndexOp>(loc, val));
    1304           0 :   }
    1305           0 : }
    1306             : 
    1307           0 : void getSliceSizeValues(DynamicGatherOp* /*dGather*/, OpBuilder& builder,

    1314           0 :     Value idx = builder.create<arith::ConstantIndexOp>(loc, i);
    1315           0 :     sliceSizeValues.push_back(
    1316           0 :         builder.create<tensor::ExtractOp>(loc, sliceSizes, idx));
    1317           0 :   }

    1319             : 
    1320             : // Verify the following properties:
    1321             : //  P1. Verify no repeat in start_index_map.

    3721             : // Checks the following eligibility criteria for compact printing of reduce:
    3722             : // E1. The reduce-op wraps a single inner-op in the associated region.
    3723             : // E2. The single operation is a commutative binary-op from the dialect, zero
    3724             : //     region, producing single result such that the operands and result all
    3725             : //     have the same type.
    3726             : // E3. The reduce-op consist of at least one input-operand; The operand-types of
    3727             : //     inner-op should be derived trivially from the element-type of reduce-op's
    3728             : //     first input-operand.
    3729             : // E4. The  arguments of the region's only basic block are forwarded perfectly
    3730             : //     to inner-op's operands.
    3731             : // E5. The reduce-op, inner-op, blocks arguments, and the return-op all have the
    3732             : //     same location.
    3733             : // E6. The single operation result is perfectly forwarded to the reduce op
    3734             : //     return.
